## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. Classical nonlinear oscillator models include Duffing, van der Pol, and driven/damped variants with polynomial or trigonometric nonlinearities in x and v.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping dependent on position)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Parametrically driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity-dependent damping)
- Cubic damping oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity damping)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric + symmetric nonlinear restoring)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v + c2 * x**2 * v (cross-coupling terms)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced Duffing oscillator)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (quadratic nonlinear restoring + damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Symmetric restoring force (even potential) ŌåÆ only odd powers of x: c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*x**5
- Asymmetric potential ŌåÆ even powers of x appear: c0*x + c1*x**2 in the force
- Self-sustained oscillation ŌåÆ nonlinear damping terms like v*(1 - x**2) or v**3 that can supply/remove energy
- Hardening/softening spring ŌåÆ sign of cubic coefficient x**3: positive = hardening, negative = softening
- Autonomous system (no explicit time) ŌåÆ dv_dt depends only on x and v, suggesting conservative or dissipative dynamics
- Periodic driving ŌåÆ presence of sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms in acceleration
- Energy-dependent damping ŌåÆ velocity terms multiplied by functions of x┬▓ + v┬▓ (amplitude-dependent dissipation)
- Phase-space polynomial structure ŌåÆ acceleration as multivariate polynomial in (x, v) for smooth nonlinear systems
